CENTRAL BANK OF CHILE
Santiago                                                      SAL It
sECoND STRUC=URAL ADJUSMENT -WAN: BACKGROUND TO INPLDMENTATION OF THE PROGRAM
I.        8coPe of the Protram
tntroduction
1.        In 1985, as may be seen from the Project Completion Report on
Structural Adjustment Loan No. I, the Chilean economy began to lay a firm
foundation from which to promote export-based growth and a higher domestic
savings rate, and thereby reduce its dependence on external financing. Thus,
the initial stage of the country's structural adjustment program can be
described as successful. In early 1986. in view of its need to make that
foundation firmer still, Chile applied to the World Bank for funding support
in the form of a second structural adjustment leanding operation that would
guarantee the financial viability of the new adjustment phase then beginning.
Priorities
2.        In order to ensure that this second phase would consolidate the
country's ultimate objective, the priorities of the new adjustment program
were:  to progress with the reprivatization and recapitalixation of the
banking and corporate sectors; to raise the public savings rate to 4.4X of
GDP; to promote an efficient austerity-based program of government spending;
and, finally, to strengthen both export incentives and social programs.
3.        In particular, this adjustment program was intended to foster the
development of a safe and efficient capital market by instituting measures
that would facilitate: recapitalization of the nonfinancial private sector,
through case-by-case renegotiation with viable debtors who were experiencing
problems; recapitalization of the banking system; and, finally,
reprivatisation of the banks in whose management the authorities had
intervened. In addition, it was proposed to introduce new banking legislation
that would ensure greater transparency in the management of these institutions
and facilitate the process of supervising them.
4.        The adjustment program ws also designed to enable Chile to reach
its set goal of an increase in public sector savings by reinforcing its policy
of accountability and austerity in current expenditure, initiated in 1985, a
policy more intent on incre. sing employment opportunities than on wage
improvements impossible to be sustained into the medium term. A further
program aim was to continue adding to the efficiency of government capital
spending through large-scale projects in the copper and energy sectors and
medium-scale infrastructure projects that would pave the way for direct
development of export activities and efficient import substitution.
5.        in addition, the program included provisions for strengthening
export incentives by: maintaining a stable and realistic exchange policy;
continuing with the Copper Stabilization Fund program; increasing individual



AMuR 5
Page 14 of 36
- 233 -
exporters' bank credit margins; completion and issue of a study on medium- and
long-term investment requirements in the forestry sector; and, finally,
improving the support made available through PROCHILE to small and medium
exporters of nontraditional products.
6.        Finally, given the need to focus social expenditure more
efficiently, the adjustment program called for implementation of a plan to
decentralize administration of the country's key social programs. It also
sought to solve the shortage of financial and infrastructure resources evident
in the health sector by raising wage-earners' obligatory social security
contributions and developing a plan of action for utilizing available hospital
facilities more rationally in the future.
Role of the IMF. the World Dank and other sources of financing
7.        At the beginning of 1986, since the specific quantitative goals set
for 198S under the EFF program had been reached, the IMP decided to contisue
with it so as to support the new phase of structural adjustment that was
beginning. The key EFF'objective for this stage, besides further advances in
reducing the current account deficit against a background of moderate economic
growth and declining inflation, was to implement a monetary policy of avoiding
new subsidies to the banking system and phasing out current ones and to follow
a fiscal policy that would lead to an additional reduction in the consolidated
public-sector deficit. To these ends, as in 1985, the EFF program delineated
a set of specific quantitative limits for 1986.
S.        The World Bank officially approved a further US$250 mdllion
structural adjustment loan (SAL II) for the period 1986-87 in November 1986.
These funds, intended to support the measures introduced in 1986 and the first
half of 1987, were to be disbursed in two tranches - the first, for US$150
million, to be payable immediately on signature of the loan agreement
(November 1986) -  with the second, for US$100 million, to be subject to the
fulfillment of certain pre-established conditions (June 1987). At the same
time. the external debt negotiations referred to in the Project Completion
Report on SAL I made provision for rescheduling commitments that matured in
1987 and repricing the outstanding debt as of January 1, 1987. In addition,
although the arrangements to finance the 1987 balance of payments shortfall
did not include seeking fresh money from the international financial
community, they did include negotiations for a retiming of interest payments,
by changing their frequency from a six-monthly to a twelve-monthly basis, as
of January 1, 1987. Ul
II.       Scone of the Program
Policy imoletentation
9.        Beginning in mid-1986, on completion of an evaluation period on the
most efficient strategy for ensuring development of a competitive and stable
capital market over the medium term, key measures for a real strengthening in
I/ Because of the delays which affected these negotiations, the retiming
came into effect only as of January 1, ;988, which meant that the Chilean
authorities found it necessary to raise a US$225 million bridge loan with
the Bank for International Settlement in 1987.



ANNEX 5
Page 15 of 36
- 234 -
the equity position of the banking system were implemented. At the same time,
in order to extend the advances made in 1985 in improving equilibrium in both
external and domestic accounts, the policies focused on raising the public
savings rate ad preserving the competitiveness of sectors producing tradable
goods were reinforced. Proof of the success of these moves is to be seen in
the fact that the program agreed on with the World Bank for this second phase
was implemented in its entirety. As an examination of the accompanying
Table I will show, the conditions agreed on for disbursement of the second
tranche of SAL 1I were complied with fully by April 1987.
Macroeconomic results
10.       As a consequence of implementation of the policies described, the
progress that had been achieved over the course of 1985 with the country's
external and domestic accounts began to take an obviously firm hold in 1986.
Not only was there a further - and, again, significant - adjustment In the
level of domestic expenditure, but economic activity continued to show
moc irate but sustained growth based on exports, with an additional domestic
savings effort. Specifically, the current account deficit was 182 lower than
in 1985, which meant that the goal of bringing aggregate expenditure to
approximately US$1 billion was successfully achieved (refer to Table 2).
11.       In addition, Chile's dependence on external financing continued
falling significantly in 1986: with moderately higher investment rates,
national gross savings rose from 5.4S of GDP to 7.7S. As indicated by the
change in the rate of government savings, which rose from 3.82 of GDP to 4.42
over the same period, the public sector continued to be responsible for a
major part of this additional effort. This contributed decisively once again
to the real improvement observed in the deficit of the nonfinancial public
sector, which fe-1 from 2.6% of GDP in 1985 to 22 in 1986 (refer to Table 4).
Projected and actual performance
12.       In 1986, macroeconomic indicators behaved very much in accordance
with officiil mid-year projections, 2/ repeating the pattern of the preceding
period. The deficit in the balance of payments current account was almost
exactly at the level predicted, despite slight but exactly offsetting
underestimates of payments for financial services and the trade account
surplus (refer to Table 2). As to the elements that determine the latter, it
is to be noted that noncopper export volume was less than predicted, but
examination of the key assumptions listed in Table 3 shows this to have been
due mainly to significant und .estimaticon of the volume growth rates of the
major nontraditional export products. Projections for the other key
assumptions regarding the external sector were fairly accurate.
13.       The growth rate in activity level was underestimated by a L.ittle
over one percentage point, mainly because of unexpected increases in both
investment and exports. Aggregate consumption, however, was projected
accurately. Regarding 1987, while the activity level showed a slightly higher
2/   These projections are to be found in an unpublished document completed by
the Research Department of the Central Bank of Chile on August 6, 1986.
They reflect the base scenario (i.e. "zero") which this document presents.

than estimated growth rate as a result of unrerestimation of consumption
levels, the deficit in the balance of payments current account was clearly
more positive than predicted, a result traceable essentially not only to the
unexpected inqLaee, noted from early 1987 onward, in the price of copper
(which rose by nearly 1002 from December 1986 to December 1987) but also to
underestimation of the rate of growth in the volumes of copper exported; these
improvements would have translated into a considerably reduced current account
deficit bad there not been a significant (approxitmtely 202) underestimate of
Imports during the period, explained mainly by an increase in imports of
capital goods.

Central Bank of Chile
Santiago                                           SAL III
THIRD STRUCTURAL ADJUSTMENT LOAN: BACKGROUND TO INPLEMENTATZON
I.        Scope of the Proaram
Backtround
1.        As shown by the report on SAL II, in 1986 Chile's economy continued
to lay the bases for sustained growth in production and employmeat, along with
a gradual improveent in external accounts and a reduction in the relative
weight of the external debt. As such, that second phase of the structural
adjustment program can also be considered successful.
In early 1987, owing to the need to consolidate those bases, the
World Bank was approached for addltional credit in the form of a third SAL
operation to provide a large share of the necessary financing.
Priorities
2.        As indicated, SAL III essentially continued to build on the progress
since 1985 regarding structural adjustment in production and expenditure. The
program also included the introduction of specific policies aimed at
fine-tuning and strengthening the incentives in each of the main areas on
which the previous programs focused - exports, investment and savings.
Lastly, the program placed special emphasis on the social sectors, to ensure
that the adjustment efforts would continue to go hand in hand with a gradual
improvement in the standard of living of the poorest segment of the population.
3.        Thus, for exports, the adjustment program continued to stress the
need to maintain e favorable macroeconomic picture by developing the sectors
with export potential. In tandem, new tax and other measures were promoted to
help neutralize the disincentives arising from customs duties and other
distortions. In brief, the specific policies and measures were: maintenance
of a stable and realistic exchange policy; maintenance of a customs policy
with low and uniform rates; maintenance and Improvement of the Copper
Stabllization Fund; and, lastly, promulgation and/or implementation of various
legal initiatives seeking to improve the drawback system for minor exports,
incorporate "indirect exporters" into the custom rebate system for imported
capital goods and inputs, and establish a partial guarantee fund for small and
medium exporters.
4.        In fiscal policy, the program continued to seek both an increase in
public savings and maintenance of a high rate of investment. Efforts were
made to raise the public savings rate from 4.82 to 52 of GDP before the
pertinent accounting corrections were made when the public enterprises were
privatized and the temporary status of government workers regulated. The
program sought to maintain public investment at 7.51 of GDP, and care was
taken to ensure that it was based on rigorous socioeconomic analysis of
projects.



- 243 -                        Page2 ofx 
5.        Under SAL III, there vas also a need for a set of incentives to
stimulate savings and private investment. Basic tools in this were the
maintenance of a climate of macroeconomic stability and a tax system with the
fewest disinceatives possible for savings and investment. In addition, owing
to its clear Impact on the volume and quality of investment, the program paid
special attention to the institutionality of the capital market. In
particular, SAL III included the full implementation of the provisions of the
recently revised Banking Law with a view to spurring competition in the
capital market; introduction of tax initiatives to aid the development of the
capital market; and, lastly, carrying out of studies and measures oimed at
improving the regulations governing institutional investors such as pension
fund administrators (AFPs, insurance companies and mutual funds.
6.        In forecasting, the adjustment program sought to carry forward a
number of actions centered on improving the new pension system. It also
sought to keep the public better informed about the features of the system nd
examined ways of lowering its operating costs.
7.        Lastly, the adjustment program sought to make bealth expenditurea
more productive by building on progress in maternal and child health;
Improving the strategy for the forecasting and prompt diagnosis of certain
chronic illnesses; making better use of the funds allocated to the national
health system; improving the new private health system (ISAPRRS)9 ad, lastly,
increasing the productivity of certain public investments in the sector,
particularly regarding the maintenance and rehabilitation of equipumnt.
Role of the IMF, World Bank and other sources of financing
8.        In early 1987, following the full achievement of the specific
quantitative targets set for 1986 by the EFF program, the International
Monetary Fund decided to proceed with its disbursements as scheduled, thereby
producing firm support for the new consolidation phase described above. 1I to
that end, as in the preceding two-year period, the program continued to set
limits for 1987 regarding the increase in the net domestic assets of the
Central Bank, international reserves and nonfinancial public sector deficit as
a proportion of GD!.
9.        In addition, financing of the 1987-88 program included funds secured
in the 1987 negotiations with the creditor banks and multilateral and
government lending agencies. Thus, the international banks participated
through retiming of interest payments from a six-monthly base to an annual one
as of January 1, 1988; the repricing of the interest rate as of January 1,
1987, eliminating the prime base determining the rate for "new money" borrowed
by the Central Bank and lowering the LIBOR margins for both now money and
original debt; the refinancing of loans amounting to US$12.486 billion, whicb
meant that all bank credits current in 1983 and new money contracted since
that time would not fall due until 1991; and, lastly, the effectiveness of the
availability of short-term co mercial credit was extended until the end of
1989 for a minimum of US$1.700 billion.
1/   The last EFF disbursement for SDR 750 million which was negotiated for
1985-87 was made in August 1988, when it was increased by SDR 7S million.

pre-established conditions (December 1988). 21
Scope of the Program
Implementation of Policies
11.       During the second half of 1987, as a test of the resolve to promote
the consolidation of the recent progress in structural adjustment, a set of
initiatives aimed at strengthening the export sector, increasing the quality
and quantity of investment and increasing domestic savings was implemented.
At the same time, to continue the progress made in recent years in the social
arena. policies seeking to raise the efficiency of both the new pension and
private health systems as well as health sector funding were strengthened.
Testimony to the foregoing is the full implementation of the program agreed
with the World Bank for this third phase. As can be seen from Table I below,
the specific measures agreed for the disbursement of the second tranche under
the SAL ITI loan were fully implemented by October 1988.
2/   In December 1988 only US$ll2.4 million was disbursed, and the balance of
the original tranche (i.e. US$12.6 million) was disbursed in early 1989.

Macroeconomic results
12.       In 1987. as a result of the policies described, the progress that
had been made .ince 1985 in external and national accounts was consolidated in
large measure, thereby satisfying the main objectives of the third phase of
the adjustment program. In point of fact, together with an additional
adjustment in the level of domestic expenditure, there continued to be a
moderate - but sustained - increase based on exports end a simultaneous rise
in domestic savings. The current account deficit in the balance of payments
was 261 lower than in 1986, following a marked improvement in the trade
balance and lover payments for financial services than originally projected
(see Table 2).
13.       Reliance on external financing continued to decline in 1987. The
rate of investment increased and gross domestic savings rose from 7. 7  to
12.61 of GDP (see Table 4). The rise in public savings in the same period
from 5.51 to 5.81 of GDP meant that a nonnegligable share of the increase was
attributable to the public sector. That increase had a major impact on the
deficit of the nonfinancial public sector, which decreased from 1.71 of GDP in
1986 to 0.25S of GDP in 1987.
14.       Preliminary figures show that in 1988 significant progress was made
in external and national accounts. In particular, while activity expanded by
6.81, a rate of growth that had not been achieved since the beginning of the
decade, the current account deficit was nearly one third of the billion
dollars that had been set as a target in mid-1987. Moreover, these results
were accompanied by an additional reduction in reliance on external financing
since, with a rate of investment equal to that in 1987, gross dpnestic savings
rose from 12.6X to 15S of GDP. That progreFs clearly had a favorable impact
on the prices for the major exports, especially copper. As a result of the
structural adjustment programs previously agreed with the World Bank, a
significant share of the additional income derived from higher copper prices
was accumulated in the Stabilization Fund established for that purpose.
Proiected and actual performance
15.       In 1987 macroeconomic accounts were sounder than officially
projected mid-year. Thus, the current account deficit in the balance of
payments was lower than projected, owing primarily to better performance of
the trade balance than originally expected (Table 2). Regarding the
determinants of the latter, there was a significant underestimating of both
copper and noncopper exports, which far exceeded that for imports. In this
connection, the performance of the key assumptions in Table 3 shows that the
behavior of exports was due to a sharp and unexpected increase in prices for
the major exports, as indicated above, which in turn was supported by a
doubling of the rate of growth projected for noncopper products. Specifically
for copper exports, the underestimating of prices mentioned above reached a
significant 26X, whereas projections on volume were very accurate.
16.       Moreover, in 1987, growth in the level of activity was
underestimated by somewhat more than one-half of a percentage point,
essentially due to an unforeseen -- and significant -- increase in the rate of
investment. The projection regarding aggregate consumption in that year was
very accurate. For 1988, while the level of activity grew significantly



-252                            ANNEX 5
Page 33 of 36
faster than estimated because the increase in consumption was underestimated
(6.1 percentage points), the actual current account deficit was only one third
of the projected level (see Table 2). This was due to a significant
underestimatin$.of exports that more than offset that, albeit also high, for
imports. Regarding the estimates of prices and exportable volumes, these
behaved in essentially the same manner as in 1987, although this time the
underestimating of copper prices was of a much higher magnitude, i.e. 73%.
